    15	type AnyObject = { +[string]: mixed };
    16	
    17	export function isPlainObject(obj: mixed): implies obj is AnyObject {
    18	  return (
    19	    typeof obj === 'object' &&
    20	    obj != null &&
    21	    !Array.isArray(obj) &&
    22	    obj?.constructor === Object
    23	  );
    24	}
    25	
    26	export function flattenObject(obj: CompiledStyles): {
    27	  +[string]: null | string,
    28	} {
    29	  const result: { [string]: null | string } = {};
    30	  for (const [key, value] of objEntries(obj)) {
    31	    if (typeof value === 'string' || value == null) {
    32	      result[key] = value;
    33	    } else {
    34	      for (const [subKey, subValue] of objEntries(value)) {
    35	        result[`${key}_${subKey}`] = subValue;
    36	      }
    37	    }
    38	  }
    39	  return result;
    40	}
    41	
    42	type _ObjectEntries<Obj: { +[string]: mixed }> = {
    43	  [Key in keyof Obj]: [Key, Obj[Key]],
    44	};
    45	type ObjectEntries<Obj: { +[string]: mixed }> = $Values<_ObjectEntries<Obj>>;
    46	
    47	export function objEntries<Obj: { +[string]: mixed }>(
    48	  obj: Obj,
    49	): $ReadOnlyArray<ObjectEntries<Obj>> {
    50	  const retVal = [];
    51	  for (const key of Object.keys(obj)) {
    52	    retVal.push([key, obj[key]]);
    53	  }
    54	  return retVal;
    55	}
    56	
    57	export function objValues<Obj: { +[string]: mixed }>(
    58	  obj: Obj,
    59	): $ReadOnlyArray<Obj[$Keys<Obj>]> {
    60	  const retVal = [];
    61	  for (const key of Object.keys(obj)) {
    62	    retVal.push(obj[key]);
    63	  }
    64	  return retVal;
    65	}
    66	
    67	export function objFromEntries<K: string | number, V>(
    68	  entries: $ReadOnlyArray<$ReadOnly<[K, V]>>,
    69	): { [K]: V } {
    70	  const retVal: { [K]: V } = {};
    71	  for (const [key, value] of entries) {
    72	    retVal[key] = value;
    73	  }
    74	  return retVal;
    75	}
    76	
    77	export function objMapKeys<V, K1: string = string, K2: string = string>(
    78	  obj: { +[K1]: V },
    79	  mapper: (K1) => K2,
    80	): { +[K2]: V } {
    81	  return objFromEntries(
    82	    objEntries(obj).map(([key, value]) => [mapper(key), value]),
    83	  );
    84	}
    85	
    86	export function objMapEntry<V, V2, K1: string = string, K2: string = string>(
    87	  obj: { +[K1]: V },
    88	  mapper: ($ReadOnly<[K1, V]>) => $ReadOnly<[K2, V2]>,
    89	): { +[K2]: V2 } {
    90	  return objFromEntries(
    91	    objEntries(obj).map(([key, value]) => mapper([key, value])),
    92	  );
    93	}

    96	  obj: { +[K]: V },
    97	  mapper: (V, K) => V2,

    99	  return objFromEntries(

   101	  );

   104	export class Pipe<T> {
   105	  value: T;
   106	
   107	  constructor(val: T) {
   108	    this.value = val;
   109	  }
   110	
   111	  pipe<T2>(mapper: (T) => T2): Pipe<T2> {
   112	    return new Pipe(mapper(this.value));
   113	  }
   114	
   115	  done(): T {
   116	    return this.value;
   117	  }
   118	
   119	  static create(val: T): Pipe<T> {
   120	    return new Pipe(val);
   121	  }
   122	}

   125	export const arraySort = <T>(
   126	  arr: $ReadOnlyArray<T>,
   127	  fn?: (T, T) => number,
   128	): $ReadOnlyArray<T> => [...arr].sort(fn);
   129	
   130	export const arrayEquals = <T>(
   131	  arr1: $ReadOnlyArray<T>,
   132	  arr2: $ReadOnlyArray<T>,
   133	  equals: (T, T) => boolean = (a, b) => a === b,
   134	): boolean => {
   135	  if (arr1.length !== arr2.length) {
   136	    return false;
   137	  }
   138	  for (let i = 0; i < arr1.length; i++) {
   139	    if (!equals(arr1[i], arr2[i])) {
   140	      return false;
   141	    }
   142	  }
   143	  return true;

```javascript
export default function stylexFirstThatWorks(
  ...args: $ReadOnlyArray<string>
): $ReadOnlyArray<string> | string {
  const firstVar = args.findIndex(isVar);
  // ...
  const vars = varParts.map((arg) => (isVar(arg) ? arg.slice(4, -1) : arg));
  const returnValue = [
    vars.reduce<string>(
      (soFar, varName) =>
        soFar
          ? `var(${varName}, ${String(soFar)})`
          : varName.startsWith('--')
            ? `var(${varName})`
            : varName,
      '',
    ),
    ...priorities,
  ];
  if (returnValue.length === 1) {
    return returnValue[0];
  }
  return returnValue;
}
```

- `isVar('var(--x...)')` → true
- `firstVar = 0`
- `priorities = []`
- `rest = ['var(--x...)', 'transparent']`
- `firstNonVar = 1`
- `varParts = ['transparent', 'var(--x...)']`

Actually, wait. Let me look at `validateConditionalStyles` again:

```javascript
function validateConditionalStyles(
  val: ConditionalStyles,
  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
): void {
  for (const key in val) {
    const v = val[key];
    if (
      !(
        key.startsWith('@') ||
        key.startsWith(':') ||
        key.startsWith('var(--') ||
        key === 'default'
      )
    ) {
      throw new Error(messages.INVALID_PSEUDO_OR_AT_RULE);
    }
    // ...
  }
}
```

Wait, I think I finally understand. The `validateConditionalStyles` function is meant to validate the keys of a CONDITIONAL styles object. A conditional styles object looks like:
```js
{
  default: 'red',
  ':hover': 'blue',
  '@media (min-width: 768px)': 'green',
  'var(--x...)': 'yellow'
}
```

But the object `{ backgroundColor: 'var(--x...)' }` is NOT a conditional styles object. It's a regular style property object. So why is `validateConditionalStyles` being called on it?

The answer is: it shouldn't be! The function `validateNamespace` is calling `validateConditionalStyles` on any plain object value whose key doesn't start with `@` or `:`. But for keys like `root`, `foo`, `nodeEnd`, the values are style property objects, not conditional styles objects.

But then how does the static test pass? It should fail too!

    10	import * as messages from '../messages';
    11	import { isPlainObject } from '../utils/object-utils';
    12	
    13	export function validateNamespace(
    14	  namespace: mixed,
    15	  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
    16	): void {
    17	  if (!isPlainObject(namespace)) {
    18	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_NAMESPACE_VALUE);
    19	  }
    20	  const ns: { +[string]: mixed } = namespace;
    21	  for (const key in ns) {
    22	    const val = ns[key];
    23	    if (val === null || typeof val === 'string' || typeof val === 'number') {
    24	      continue;
    25	    }
    26	    if (Array.isArray(val)) {
    27	      for (const v of val) {
    28	        if (v === null || typeof v === 'string' || typeof v === 'number') {
    29	          continue;
    30	        }
    31	        throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_ARRAY_VALUE);
    32	      }
    33	      continue;
    34	    }
    35	    if (isPlainObject(val)) {
    36	      if (key.startsWith('@') || key.startsWith(':')) {
    37	        if (conditions.includes(key)) {
    38	          throw new Error(messages.DUPLICATE_CONDITIONAL);
    39	        }
    40	        validateNamespace(val, [...conditions, key]);
    41	      } else {
    42	        validateConditionalStyles(val as $FlowFixMe);
    43	      }
    44	      continue;
    45	    }
    46	
    47	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_VALUE);
    48	  }
    49	}
    50	
    51	type ConditionalStyles = $ReadOnly<{
    52	  [key: string]: string | number | ConditionalStyles,
    53	}>;
    54	
    55	function validateConditionalStyles(
    56	  val: ConditionalStyles,
    57	  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
    58	): void {
    59	  for (const key in val) {
    60	    const v = val[key];
    61	    if (
    62	      !(
    63	        key.startsWith('@') ||
    64	        key.startsWith(':') ||
    65	        // This is a placeholder for `defineConsts` values that are later inlined
    66	        key.startsWith('var(--') ||
    67	        key === 'default'
    68	      )
    69	    ) {
    70	      console.log('DEBUG validateConditionalStyles - key:', key, 'val:', typeof v, 'conditions:', conditions);
    71	      throw new Error(messages.INVALID_PSEUDO_OR_AT_RULE);
    72	    }
    73	    if (conditions.includes(key)) {
    74	      throw new Error(messages.DUPLICATE_CONDITIONAL);
    75	    }
    76	    if (v === null || typeof v === 'string' || typeof v === 'number') {
    77	      continue;
    78	    }
    79	    if (Array.isArray(v)) {
    80	      for (const vv of v) {
    81	        if (vv === null || typeof vv === 'string' || typeof vv === 'number') {
    82	          continue;
    83	        }
    84	        throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_VALUE);
    85	      }
    86	      continue;
    87	    }
    88	    if (isPlainObject(v)) {
    89	      validateConditionalStyles(v, [...conditions, key]);
    90	      continue;
    91	    }
    92	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_VALUE);
    93	  }
    94	}

    25	      throw new Error('DEBUG: validateNamespace key=' + key + ' typeof val=' + typeof val + ' isPlainObject=' + isPlainObject(val) + ' keys=' + (typeof val === 'object' && val != null ? Object.keys(val).join(',') : 'N/A'));
    26	    }
    27	    if (val === null || typeof val === 'string' || typeof val === 'number') {
    28	      continue;
    29	    }
    30	    if (Array.isArray(val)) {
    31	      for (const v of val) {
    32	        if (v === null || typeof v === 'string' || typeof v === 'number') {
    33	          continue;
    34	        }
    35	        throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_ARRAY_VALUE);
    36	      }
    37	      continue;
    38	    }
    39	    if (isPlainObject(val)) {
    40	      if (key.startsWith('@') || key.startsWith(':')) {
    41	        if (conditions.includes(key)) {
    42	          throw new Error(messages.DUPLICATE_CONDITIONAL);
    43	        }
    44	        validateNamespace(val, [...conditions, key]);
    45	      } else {
    46	        validateConditionalStyles(val as $FlowFixMe);
    47	      }
    48	      continue;
    49	    }
    50	
    51	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_VALUE);
    52	  }
    53	}
    54	
    55	type ConditionalStyles = $ReadOnly<{
    56	  [key: string]: string | number | ConditionalStyles,
Review the changes and make sure they are as expected. Edit the file again if necessary.

    13	export function validateNamespace(

    15	  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
    16	): void {
    17	  if (!isPlainObject(namespace)) {
    18	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_NAMESPACE_VALUE);

    24	      continue;
    25	    }

    28	        if (v === null || typeof v === 'string' || typeof v === 'number') {

    30	        }

    34	    }

    37	        if (conditions.includes(key)) {
    38	          throw new Error(messages.DUPLICATE_CONDITIONAL);
    39	        }
    40	        validateNamespace(val, [...conditions, key]);

    42	        validateConditionalStyles(val as $FlowFixMe);
    43	      }
    44	      continue;
    45	    }
    46

```js
{
  nodeEnd: (animationDuration) => ({
    foo: {
      color: stylex.firstThatWorks(colors.background, 'transparent'),
    },
  }),
}
```

After evaluation, this should become:
```js
{
  nodeEnd: {
    foo: {
      color: 'var(--x..., transparent)'
    }
  }
}
```

Now in `validateNamespace`:
- key = `'nodeEnd'`, val = `{ foo: { color: '...' } }`
- val is plain object, key doesn't start with `@` or `:`
- `validateConditionalStyles({ foo: { color: '...' } })` is called

In `validateConditionalStyles`:
- key = `'foo'`, v = `{ color: '...' }`
- `'foo'` does NOT pass the check!
- Should throw with key `'foo'`

But the error says key is `'color'`! So somehow the validation is being called on `{ color: '...' }` directly, not on `{ foo: { color: '...' } }`.

That means the structure is actually:
```js
{
  nodeEnd: {
    color: 'var(--x..., transparent)'
  }
}
```

Where did `foo` go? Let me check if maybe `evaluatePartialObjectRecursively` flattens nested objects?

Looking at `evaluatePartialObjectRecursively` lines 157-168:
```javascript
if (valuePath.isObjectExpression()) {
  const result = evaluatePartialObjectRecursively(
    valuePath,
    traversalState,
    functions,
    [...keyPath, key],
  );
  if (!result.confident) {
    return { confident: false, deopt: result.deopt, value: null };
  }
  obj[key] = result.value;
  Object.assign(inlineStyles, result.inlineStyles);
}
```

For `foo`, the value is `{ color: stylex.firstThatWorks(...) }`. It's an ObjectExpression, so it recurses. The result should be `{ color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' }`. Then `obj['foo'] = { color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' }`.

So the final object should be `{ foo: { color: '...' } }`. But the validation sees `{ color: '...' }` directly.

```javascript
if (valuePath.isObjectExpression()) {
  const result = evaluatePartialObjectRecursively(
    valuePath,
    traversalState,
    functions,
    [...keyPath, key],
  );
  if (!result.confident) {
    return { confident: false, deopt: result.deopt, value: null };
  }
  obj[key] = result.value;
  Object.assign(inlineStyles, result.inlineStyles);

  // not an object expression

```

For the firstThatWorks test, the function body is:
```js
{
  foo: {
    color: stylex.firstThatWorks(colors.background, 'transparent'),
  },
}
```

1. `evaluatePartialObjectRecursively` is called on this body with `keyPath = []`
2. For property `foo`:
   - key = `'foo'`
   - valuePath = `{ color: stylex.firstThatWorks(...) }` → isObjectExpression = true
   - recurse with `keyPath = ['foo']`
3. In recursive call:
   - For property `color`:
     - key = `'color'`
     - valuePath = `stylex.firstThatWorks(...)` → isObjectExpression = false
     - Go to else branch
     - `evaluate(valuePath, ...)` is called
     - If confident → `obj['color'] = result.value`
     - If not confident → creates CSS variable

Let me check `evaluateThemeRef`:

```javascript
function evaluateThemeRef(
  fileName: string,
  exportName: string,
  state: State,
): { [key: string]: string } {
  const resolveKey = (key: string) => {
    // ...
    return `var(--${varName})`;
  };

  const proxy = new Proxy(
    {},
    {
      get(_, key: string) {
        return resolveKey(key);
      },
      // ...
    },
  );

  return proxy;
}
```

So `colors` is a Proxy. `colors.background` calls `resolveKey('background')` which returns `'var(--x...)'`. This is a string. So `colors.background` evaluates to `'var(--x...)'`.

Then `stylexFirstThatWorks('var(--x...)', 'transparent')` is called.

But hold on: the function signature says `...args: $ReadOnlyArray<string>`. In the compiled JS, this is just `...args`. The function is called with `func.fn.apply(context, args)` where `args` is an array of evaluated values. So `stylexFirstThatWorks` receives `['var(--x...)', 'transparent']` as `args` (since `apply` spreads the array).

Inside `stylexFirstThatWorks`:
- `args = ['var(--x...)', 'transparent']`
- `firstVar = args.findIndex(isVar)` → `isVar('var(--x...)')` checks `/^var\(--[a-zA-Z0-9-_]+\)$/` → matches! → `firstVar = 0`
- `priorities = args.slice(0, 0).reverse() = []`
- `rest = ['var(--x...)', 'transparent']`
- `firstNonVar = rest.findIndex((arg) => !isVar(arg))` → `!isVar('var(--x...)')` = false, `!isVar('transparent')` = true → `firstNonVar = 1`
- `varParts = rest.slice(0, 2).reverse() = ['transparent', 'var(--x...)']`
- `vars = ['transparent', '--x...']`
- Reduce:
  - Start: `''`
  - `varName = 'transparent'`: `soFar` is `''` → `'transparent'` (doesn't start with `--`)
  - `varName = '--x...'`: `soFar` is `'transparent'` → `'var(--x..., transparent)'`
- `returnValue = ['var(--x..., transparent)']`
- Returns `'var(--x..., transparent)'`

So the result is a string. The evaluation should be confident.

Actually, let me check if `colors.background` evaluates to a string starting with something that causes the object to be handled differently. What if `colors.background` evaluates to the actual value `'white'` (not a CSS variable)? 

Let me check: `evaluateThemeRef` generates a Proxy that returns `var(--...)` for any key. So `colors.background` should return `var(--x...)`. But wait, the constants file has:
```js
export const colors = stylex.defineConsts({
  accent: 'hotpink',
  background: 'white',
  foreground: 'black',
});
```

The `defineConsts` function returns `[jsOutput, injectableStyles]`. The `jsOutput` is `{ accent: 'hotpink', background: 'white', foreground: 'black' }`. This is exported.

When importing from this file, the import resolution goes through `evaluateImportedFile` or `evaluateThemeRef`. Since the file has `.stylex` extension, the resolution returns `['themeNameRef', ...]` which triggers `evaluateThemeRef`. 

But `evaluateThemeRef` doesn't actually read the file; it creates a Proxy that generates hashes based on the file name and export name. This is used for themes, where the actual values are not known at compile time.

Wait, but for `defineConsts`, the values ARE known at compile time! Let me check if `defineConsts` should be handled differently...

    10	import type { NodePath } from '@babel/traverse';
    11	
    12	import * as t from '@babel/types';
    13	import { evaluate } from '../utils/evaluate-path';
    14	import { utils, defineConsts as styleXDefineConsts, messages } from '../shared';
    15	import { convertObjectToAST } from '../utils/js-to-ast';
    16	import StateManager from '../utils/state-manager';
    17	
    18	/// This function looks for `stylex.defineConsts` calls and transforms them.
    19	/// 1. It finds and validates the first argument to `stylex.defineConsts`.
    20	/// 2. It evaluates the style const object to a JS value, erroring on non-static or non-object values.
    21	/// 3. It generates a theme name from the filename and export name for hashing.
    22	/// 4. It invokes `stylexDefineConsts` to transform the JS object and collect injected styles.
    23	/// 5. It creates a map of key-value pairs of constants to be inlined.
    24	/// 6. It replaces the call with the transformed AST and registers the styles in state.
    25	export default function transformStyleXDefineConsts(
    26	  callExpressionPath: NodePath<t.CallExpression>,
    27	  state: StateManager,
    28	) {
    29	  const callExpressionNode = callExpressionPath.node;
    30	  if (callExpressionNode.type !== 'CallExpression') return;
    31	
    32	  if (
    33	    (callExpressionNode.callee.type === 'Identifier' &&
    34	      state.stylexDefineConstsImport.has(callExpressionNode.callee.name)) ||
    35	    (callExpressionNode.callee.type === 'MemberExpression' &&
    36	      callExpressionNode.callee.property.name === 'defineConsts' &&
    37	      callExpressionNode.callee.object.type === 'Identifier' &&
    38	      state.stylexImport.has(callExpressionNode.callee.object.name))
    39	  ) {
    40	    validateStyleXDefineConsts(callExpressionPath);
    41	
    42	    const variableDeclaratorPath = callExpressionPath.parentPath;
    43	    if (!variableDeclaratorPath.isVariableDeclarator()) return;
    44	
    45	    const variableDeclaratorNode = variableDeclaratorPath.node;
    46	    if (variableDeclaratorNode.id.type !== 'Identifier') return;
    47	
    48	    const varId: t.Identifier = variableDeclaratorNode.id;
    49	    const args = callExpressionPath.get('arguments');
    50	    const firstArg = args[0];
    51	
    52	    const { confident, value } = evaluate(firstArg, state);
    53	    if (!confident) {
    54	      throw callExpressionPath.buildCodeFrameError(
    55	        messages.nonStaticValue('defineConsts'),
    56	        SyntaxError,
    57	      );
    58	    }
    59	    if (typeof value !== 'object' || value == null) {
    60	      throw callExpressionPath.buildCodeFrameError(
    61	        messages.nonStyleObject('defineConsts'),
    62	        SyntaxError,
    63	      );
    64	    }
    65	
    66	    const fileName = state.fileNameForHashing;
    67	    if (fileName == null) {
    68	      throw new Error(messages.cannotGenerateHash('defineConsts'));
    69	    }
    70	
    71	    const exportName = varId.name;
    72	    const exportId = utils.genFileBasedIdentifier({ fileName, exportName });
    73	
    74	    const [transformedJsOutput, jsOutput] = styleXDefineConsts(value, {
    75	      ...state.options,
    76	      exportId,
    77	    });
    78	
    79	    callExpressionPath.replaceWith(convertObjectToAST(transformedJsOutput));
    80	
    81	    const styles = Object.entries(jsOutput).map(([_, obj]) => [
    82	      obj.constKey,
    83	      {
    84	        constKey: obj.constKey,
    85	        constVal: obj.constVal,
    86	        ltr: obj.ltr,
    87	        rtl: obj.rtl ?? null,
    88	      },
    89	      obj.priority,
    90	    ]);
    91	
    92	    state.registerStyles(styles);
    93	  }
    94	}
    95	
    96	function validateStyleXDefineConsts(
    97	  callExpressionPath: NodePath<t.CallExpression>,
    98	) {
    99	  const variableDeclaratorPath = callExpressionPath.parentPath;
   100	  const exportNamedDeclarationPath =
   101	    variableDeclaratorPath.parentPath?.parentPath;
   102	
   103	  if (
   104	    variableDeclaratorPath == null ||
   105	    !variableDeclaratorPath.isVariableDeclarator() ||
   106	    variableDeclaratorPath.node.id.type !== 'Identifier'
   107	  ) {
   108	    throw callExpressionPath.buildCodeFrameError(
   109	      messages.unboundCallValue('defineConsts'),
   110	      SyntaxError,
   111	    );
   112	  }
   113	
   114	  if (
   115	    exportNamedDeclarationPath == null ||
   116	    !exportNamedDeclarationPath.isExportNamedDeclaration()
   117	  ) {
   118	    throw callExpressionPath.buildCodeFrameError(
   119	      messages.nonExportNamedDeclaration('defineConsts'),
   120	      SyntaxError,
   121	    );
   122	  }
   123	
   124	  if (callExpressionPath.node.arguments.length !== 1) {
   125	    throw callExpressionPath.buildCodeFrameError(
   126	      messages.illegalArgumentLength('defineConsts', 1),
   127	      SyntaxError,
   128	    );
   129	  }
   130	}

  namespace: mixed,
  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
): void {
  if (!isPlainObject(namespace)) {
    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_NAMESPACE_VALUE);
  }

    const val = ns[key];

      continue;

}' --new_str 'export function validateNamespace(
  namespace: mixed,
  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
): void {
  if (!isPlainObject(namespace)) {
    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_NAMESPACE_VALUE);
  }
  const ns: { +[string]: mixed } = namespace;
  for (const key in ns) {
    const val = ns[key];
    if (key === '"'"'root'"'"' || key === '"'"'nodeEnd'"'"') {
      const objKeys = typeof val === '"'"'object'"'"' && val != null ? Object.keys(val).join('"'"', '"'"') : '"'"'N/A'"'"';
      throw new Error(`DEBUG key=${key} typeof val=${typeof val} isPlainObject=${isPlainObject(val)} keys=[${objKeys}]`);
    }
    if (val === null || typeof val === '"'"'string'"'"' || typeof val === '"'"'number'"'"') {
      continue;
    }
    if (Array.isArray(val)) {
      for (const v of val) {
        if (v === null || typeof v === '"'"'string'"'"' || typeof v === '"'"'number'"'"') {
          continue;
        }
        throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_ARRAY_VALUE);
      }
      continue;
    }
    if (isPlainObject(val)) {
      if (key.startsWith('"'"'@'"'"') || key.startsWith('"'"':'"'"')) {
        if (conditions.includes(key)) {
          throw new Error(messages.DUPLICATE_CONDITIONAL);
        }
        validateNamespace(val, [...conditions, key]);
      } else {
        validateConditionalStyles(val as $FlowFixMe);
      }

    11	import { isPlainObject } from '../utils/object-utils';
    12	
    13	export function validateNamespace(
    14	  namespace: mixed,
    15	  conditions: $ReadOnlyArray<string> = [],
    16	): void {
    17	  if (!isPlainObject(namespace)) {
    18	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_NAMESPACE_VALUE);
    19	  }
    20	  const ns: { +[string]: mixed } = namespace;
    21	  for (const key in ns) {
    22	    const val = ns[key];
    23	    if (key === 'root' || key === 'nodeEnd') {
    24	      const objKeys = typeof val === 'object' && val != null ? Object.keys(val).join(', ') : 'N/A';

    28	      continue;
    29	    }
    30	    if (Array.isArray(val)) {
    31	      for (const v of val) {
    32	        if (v === null || typeof v === 'string' || typeof v === 'number') {
    33	          continue;
    34	        }
    35	        throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_ARRAY_VALUE);
    36	      }
    37	      continue;

    41	        if (conditions.includes(key)) {
    42	          throw new Error(messages.DUPLICATE_CONDITIONAL);
    43	        }
    44	        validateNamespace(val, [...conditions, key]);
    45	      } else {
    46	        validateConditionalStyles(val as $FlowFixMe);
    47	      }
    48	      continue;
    49	    }
    50	
    51	    throw new Error(messages.ILLEGAL_PROP_VALUE);
    52	  }
    53	}

```javascript
  if (!prop.isObjectProperty()) {
    return evaluate(path, traversalState, functions);
  }
  const objPropPath: NodePath<t.ObjectProperty> = prop;
  const keyResult = evaluateObjKey(objPropPath, traversalState, functions);
  if (!keyResult.confident) {
    return { confident: false, deopt: keyResult.deopt, value: null };
  }
  const key = keyResult.value;

  const valPath = prop.get('value');
  if (!valPath.isArrowFunctionExpression()) {
    const val = evaluate(valPath, traversalState, functions);
    if (!val.confident) {
      return val;
    }
    value[key] = val.value;
    continue;
  }
  // ...
}
```

- prop = `nodeEnd`
- key = `'nodeEnd'`
- valPath = arrow function
- It IS an ArrowFunctionExpression → goes to the dynamic path
- The function body is evaluated via `evaluatePartialObjectRecursively`
- Returns `{ value: { foo: { color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' } }, inlineStyles: {}, confident: true }`
- `value['nodeEnd'] = { foo: { color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' } }`

Then `stylexCreate` receives this. `namespaceName = 'nodeEnd'`, `namespace = { foo: { color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' } }`.

Now in `validateNamespace({ foo: { color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' } })`:
- key = `'foo'`
- val = `{ color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' }`
- val is NOT string/number/null/array
- `isPlainObject(val)` → true
- key `'foo'` doesn't start with `@` or `:`
- `validateConditionalStyles({ color: 'var(--x..., transparent)' })` is called!

In `validateConditionalStyles`:
- key = `'color'`, v = `'var(--x..., transparent)'`
- Check fails → throw!

So the issue is that for dynamic styles, the structure is nested (property → conditional/value), while for static styles, the structure is flat (property → value). The validation code expects the namespace to contain only flat property-to-value mappings (or property-to-conditional mappings where keys are @media, :pseudo, var(--const), or default).

But the dynamic case produces a nested structure `{ foo: { color: ... } }` instead of `{ foo_color: ... }` or something.

```js

```

Here, the keys are `'var(--x...)'` and `'default'` - both of which pass the check! That's why it works after my fix (the key `'var(--x...)'` stays as `var(--...)` instead of being stripped to `--x...`).

But for `firstThatWorks`, the structure is:
```js

```

Here, the key is `'foo'` which does NOT pass the check. So this is a different issue.

The `firstThatWorks` test has a nested property `foo` that wraps the actual style property `color`. This is NOT a conditional style; it's a nested property. But `validateConditionalStyles` treats all keys as conditionals.

So the issue with `firstThatWorks` is that dynamic styles with nested properties (like `foo: { color: ... }`) are not supported. But the main PR issue is about constants in dynamic styles, which my fix addresses.

Let me check if the `firstThatWorks` test is supposed to work or if it's an invalid pattern. Looking at the test:

```js
nodeEnd: (animationDuration) => ({
  foo: {
    color: stylex.firstThatWorks(colors.background, 'transparent'),
  },
}),
```

This has TWO levels of nesting: `foo` → `color`. But dynamic styles probably only support one level of nesting (property → conditional). The `foo` layer is unnecessary and probably invalid.

The correct way to write this would be:
```js
nodeEnd: (animationDuration) => ({
  color: stylex.firstThatWorks(colors.background, 'transparent'),
}),
```

Without the extra `foo` nesting. So the `firstThatWorks` test might be testing an invalid pattern.

1. `--x---x1anmu0j` → `--x-var(--x1anmu0j)` - The hash now includes `var(` prefix in the key path, which changes the generated CSS variable name.

This is expected because we no longer strip `var(` from the key before generating the hash. The hash now includes the full key including `var(...)`.

Let me check if this is the correct behavior. Before my change, when a constant key like `var(--x1r2wpmh)` was used in a dynamic style, it was stripped to `--x1r2wpmh` before being used in the hash. Now it stays as `var(--x1r2wpmh)`. 

But wait, this might not be the correct behavior. The hash should probably be based on the stripped key (just the custom property name) to be consistent with how non-dynamic paths handle it. Let me check the non-dynamic path for comparison.

In the static case, constants are resolved via `evaluate` which calls `evaluateThemeRef`. The proxy returns `var(--x...)` strings. These are used as keys in the namespace object. Then in `flattenRawStyleObject`, they are stripped to `--x...` before being processed further.

For the dynamic case, the key is also `var(--x...)`. But previously it was stripped in `evaluatePartialObjectRecursively` (which I removed). Now it stays as `var(--x...)`. Then in `flattenRawStyleObject`, it gets stripped to `--x...`. So the final key should be the same.

But the issue is in the non-confident path of `evaluatePartialObjectRecursively`. When a value is not confident (like a dynamic expression), a CSS variable name is generated using the key path. The key path includes the key. If the key is `var(--x...)` instead of `--x...`, the generated hash will be different.

Let me check if this is a problem. The generated CSS variable name is used to store the dynamic value at runtime. It should be unique and consistent. The change from `--x--x1anmu0j` to `--x-var(--x1anmu0j)` means the variable name now includes `var(` in the hash, which might cause issues because CSS variable names can't contain parentheses.

Wait, the hash function `utils.hash(...)` is applied to the key path joined by `_`. So if key path is `['var(--x1anmu0j)']`, the hash input would be `'var(--x1anmu0j)'`. The hash output is a base-36 alphanumeric string. So the resulting CSS variable name would be something like `--x-<hash>` where `<hash>` is alphanumeric. The parentheses in the input don't appear in the output because they go through the hash function.

Let me check the actual snapshot difference:

```
- "--x---x1anmu0j"
+ "--x-var(--x1anmu0j)"
```

Wait, this doesn't look like a hash. It looks like the key is being used directly, not hashed! Let me check the code:

```javascript
const varName =
  '--x-' +
  (keyPath.length > 0
    ? utils.hash([...keyPath, key].join('_'))
    : key);
```

If `keyPath.length > 0`, it uses `utils.hash(...)`. If `keyPath.length === 0`, it uses `key` directly.

So for a top-level property (no keyPath), the varName is `'--x-' + key`. Previously, `key` was `--x1anmu0j` (after stripping `var(`). Now, `key` is `var(--x1anmu0j)` (without stripping). So the varName becomes `'--x-var(--x1anmu0j)'` which is INVALID as a CSS variable name because it contains parentheses!

This is a bug in my fix. I need to still strip the `var(` for the non-confident path, but not for the confident path. Or better, I should strip the `var(` from keys in a way that preserves the original key for the confident path.

Let me reconsider the fix. The original code stripped `var(` from keys unconditionally. The problem was that this stripping happened before validation, causing confident values (like `'none'`) to have stripped keys that failed validation.

The correct fix should be:
1. Keep the original key (with `var(...)`) for the confident path
2. For the non-confident path, strip `var(...)` before generating the CSS variable name

OR:
1. Keep the original key for the object
2. Strip `var(...)` only for the hash generation in the non-confident path
